Not so fun factâ„¢: mosquitos can transmit the deadly rabbit hemorrhagic fever/disease to rabbits, both wild and domestic. So if you have rabbits make sure to check if that might be a thing you need to worry about. Make sure to check if there's a rabbit hemorrhagic disease (RHD) vaccine available in your area and consider getting your rabbits vaccinated. The virus has a mortality rate of up to 100%, even of an animal survives it's still infectious for months and potentially even lifelong. It has an incubation period of usually around 72 hours and has no real treatment. If one of your rabbits gets it all of them have it and usually that means that over the span of a few days maybe up to two weeks the entire population will die horribly. Especially dangerous are shows and other events where rabbits from different places are gathered. Transmission happens through contaminated surfaces, clothing, droplets and bodily fluids. Carriers include mice, lice wild rabbits and mosquitos. If you're getting a newbie in your group make sure to quarantine them for at least 72 hours. Keep your rabbits safe everyone ğŸŒ»  Oh also: there's a secondary much rarer presentation that presents with lethargy, lack of appetite, weight loss and sometimes fever. This presentation is much rare and "only" comes with a mortality rate of 50 to 80% and can take weeks. In comparison the common presentation is fever, lethargy, bloody excrements, bloody gums, bloodshot eyes. Pretty much what the name says. I can't stress enough how contagious this is btw, if one animal is infected you will most likely lose your entire population. It's also harmless to humans in case anyone was concerned. If you suspect a possible infection with RHD call your vet and inform them of your suspicion, quarantine the affected animal, take good precautions regarding the possible spread (keep in mind you can easily spread it to the wild rodent population and screw yourself like that), do not allow visitors to the animal infected or any other rabbits, assume your entire population is infected and calm your local department for veterinary safety and diseases. I'm not saying this to cause panic but to spread information. If you've been to any events or any place with your rabbits in the past week make sure to inform all necessary people. We had an outbreak in my area a few years ago and while it was quickly well contained (including any shows, etc. were prevented for the entire year and the one following) the affected people lost their entire populations. I only know of a singular rabbit that survived out of a few hundreds. Just make sure to be careful if your area is affected

I am constantly bitten. At one stage I had bites covering my body and there were so many that my mom decided to try and count them. One day, at a party, I was in a conversation with a person that I had just met that day and he told me that he would kill his mosquitoes, and then line them up next to his bed to warn other mosquitoes not to mess with him and that this worked. Friendly tip: One teaspoon of water can breed 100 mosquitos.   So check your yard and anything that holds water ESPECIALLY old tires. You need to empty them out because if you have a mosquito problem. Chances are they are breeding in some old bucket or tire and alot of species stay close to home. IE your yard.    Also. Minnows are your best friends against mosquitos.   If you can capture a bunch of minnows then you can release them into ponds and other things that hold water all year around.   Minnows eat mosquito larva. Remember that.

Years back used to work as a farm hand.  After a week long series of rain storms a section of the farm's front area flooded a bit, had a couple inches of standing water beside the road, it was usually where we parked our cars, didn't pay much attention to it.   Another week passes and the water is still there, but now it has the single largest collection of mosquito larva I had ever seen in it.  Thousands of them, the water was *black* and constantly in motion from them, it was a terrifying amount and I was a little taken aback that the boss hasn't had us do anything about them.  So I go and ask him if he knows what they are.    He says, "they're some kind of bug, its no big deal." "Those are mosquito larva."  "...  It's going to kill the hell out of that patch of dirt, but I want you to dump half a gallon of bleach into that water." " *YOU GOT IT, BOSS.* "   I then had to dig a new drainage ditch.  The moral of the story is always pay attention to areas of stagnant water in or around your property so you don't have go Scorched Earth on these bastards.

Just a side note - Aedes Aegypti are invasive to the US, and we should totally exterminate them if we can. They're one of those species that carries disease, and eliminating them would allow the native mosquitos (which, by and large, don't carry disease) to reclaim their original niche.

Replace mosquito with any other creature that seems to be only a nuisance and the answer is likely the sameâ€¦ itâ€™s greatest purpose is to be prey.  Mosquitos supplement the diet of countless reptiles, amphibians, spiders and fish. And are in some cases an animals primary source of food. It is quite possible that without them, entire food webs and ecosystems could collapse. So there you have it.   The diseases they transmit to animals could also act as a natural population control that selectively culls weaker individuals. Letâ€™s not forget about the pollination! Awesome Video
Most of the species of mosquito that target humans are active during *sunset* and *sunrise.* So one way to avoid being swarmed is to not be outside at those times. There are still a few (as in a single digit mumber of species, at least in the US) that are active during the day or during the night, but the worst times by far are sunset and sunrise.  This is important for mosquito abatement since it determines what time of day fogging operations take place, Pesticide fog has to be applied while the mosquitos are in flight so that they will run into the droplets. If you fog at the wrong time, the most members of the target species of mosquito will be landed and resting instead of flying around.

If I recoll my old Mosquito Abatment training, there are also mosquito larva that live on the roots of plants that grow along the edges of bodies of water. This spot is well protected from typical predators like birds or fish, so jt can be difficult to control populations of these species (since a common abatement practice for water bodies involves introducing fish to eat the larvae). Instead, one tactic to consiser is replacing the host plants with different species that wonâ€™t shelter the mosquitos.

The Quranic word used for Mosquite is specifically that of a female mosquito. Of course, there is a significant wisdom in why the Quran mentions female mosquito specially. However, this wisdom came into light hundreds of years after the verse was sent down, as a result of some scientific researches. As you read in details, mosquitoes which suck peopleâ€™s blood and use it for their eggs are female mosquitoes. This is why the Quran chose the female mosquito for the similitude in order to point out to this reality.

Useless fact The elephant mosquito was the species shown in Jurassic Park ; the DNA extraction scene and also the big mozzie in Hammond's knob ( on his cane). Ironic since the species is a nectivore and would not have any blood ( dino or otherwise) in it's system. It was also a male mosquito. The mosquito specimens were sourced from the Public Health Entomology Research and Education Center in Panama City, which received a $50 donation for their services. Hammond's cane ( with the mosquito knob) was late sold for $32,000.

Jerry's question at the end leads to an interesting bit of mosquito trivia. The genus of mosquitoes that spreads malaria is called Anopheles, and the name comes from the prefix "an-" meaning "no" or "not" (like in "anarchy") and the noun "ophelos," meaning "benefit," "good" (in the noun sense, like "the public good"), or "profit" (in the financial sense). So, in a way, NGOs fighting malaria are all nonprofits engaged in a battle against a mosquito that is literally named "nonprofit"!

also to note, a good answer to what mosquitoes are 'good for' if you REALLY need to justify it to yourself:  Mosquitoes play a vital part in the food web, their sheer numbers and the speed of which they reproduce and mature ensure that MANY species, from insects, to fish, frogs, spiders, even birds and small mammals have an ensured direct food source, and the animals that feed on said mosquitoes in large numbers in turn also are consumed by larger animals.  not to mention, when they consume blood from other, far larger animals, theyre recycling nutrients from a creature they would be locked in, potentially for YEARS, back into the food web
